### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

You may get academic suspension if you are on academic probation and fail to fulfill all the requirements of your Learning Contract. The suspension is entered on your transcript as part of your academic record. You must meet with the Dean's Office, who establishes the conditions that you must meet prior to returning to Fulbright. While on suspension, you may not visit the Fulbright campus unless permission is given from the Dean’s Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for the purpose of attending relevant meetings. Suspensions typically are for one term or one academic year. A student may be suspended a maximum of two times. If you are suspended a third time, your enrolment in the program will be canceled, and you will have to apply for re-admission. The re-admission decision is made by the Dean’s Office in consultation with the appropriate members of faculty and staff. You must include with your application for re-admission a letter that addresses the reasons for your suspensions and cancellation, and the measures you have taken to address those reasons. Students who are re-admitted must also re-apply for financial aid. The first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity, is an Academic Warning. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.

<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 2]

### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

The P/NP grade system allows students to take a maximum of 8 credits (usually 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis. To do this, they need to submit a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form to the Registrar's Office before Week 4 of the term. A grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass, and these courses can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass, and no credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript, and courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back, and Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses or count toward major/minor requirements.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. • I = Incomplete: If a student is unable to complete the work in a course because of illness, family emergency, or other exceptional circumstances (see Section 12), a temporary grade of ‘I’ (Incomplete) may be awarded by the faculty until unfinished course requirements are completed. The student has until the date agreed upon with the faculty (not to exceed 6 months from the end of the course) to complete all remaining course work; otherwise, the student will be

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

You can take a maximum of 2 courses (4 credits each) on a Pass/No Pass basis in one academic year. However, Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. A grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass and can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass, no credit is granted for this result, and the NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Pass/No Pass grades are not included in the GPA calculation.

### Question 65: I've failed the GWP due to personal reasons so will it count toward the 144 maximum credits I can have?  
### Answer: 

Yes, the failed grade for the GWP will count toward the total attempted credits, but it will not be included in the GPA calculation if you choose to repeat the course. However, the repeated course will be counted toward the total attempted credits. If you repeat the course and earn a higher grade, the lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP" (repeated) and remain on the transcript. Keep in mind that you may not retake the same course for the third time unless you failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. You should consult with your Academic/Major Advisor about your program plan if you are considering taking the class for a third time.

### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

An Academic Warning is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. To receive an Academic Warning, a student will be sent a warning by the Registrar’s Office and will be required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.

### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

To major in Applied Mathematics, you would need to take a series of courses starting from foundation courses, intermediate courses, and advanced courses. Here are some examples:

Foundation Courses:
- Linear Algebra
- Single variable Calculus
- Introduction to Statistics
- Multivariable Calculus

Intermediate Courses:
- Probability
- Differential Equations
- Discrete Mathematics
- Numerical Analysis

Advanced Courses:
- Advanced Statistics
- Statistical Learning
- Stochastic Calculus
- Numerical Analysis
- Optimization
- Partial Differential Equations

You will also need to take at least 2 applied courses, one at 200 level, from other majors that emphasize the applications of Mathematics. For example, you could take Game theory, The Economics of Corruption, Money and Banking, or Economics of Inequality from Economics, or Signal, Systems, and Control, or Computer Vision from Engineering.

Consultation with an academic advisor is required for course selection. Also, note that students may not double count a course for two different requirements.

If you are considering graduate school in Economics or Finance, it would be beneficial to take courses in calculus, linear algebra, differential equations, and real analysis. You should also set up a meeting with an advisor in Economics to determine precisely which courses will be essential for your chosen graduate program.

### Question 69: How to declare a major in Computer Science?  
### Answer: 

To declare Computer Science as their major, a student must complete at least two Computer Science courses. This includes MATH 202 - Discrete Math and at least one other Computer Science course. The student must also meet the requirements for the major, which include completing certain courses in Computer Science at the intermediate and advanced levels, as well as completing a capstone project. Additionally, the student must meet the school's policy for experiential learning if applicable.

As part of the major, students will be equipped with the foundational knowledge in Computer Science and relevant disciplines. ### Question 70: I'm currently under a General Work Program for Experiential Learning but the company do not pay me in any form. How can I get the subsidy from Fulbright University?  
### Answer: 

The Fulbright University's Experiential Learning Program (ELP) does provide subsidies for eligible students. However, the program requires that students complete their experiential learning under a paid position. Since you mentioned that the company does not pay you in any form, it seems that you are not currently eligible for the subsidy under the ELP. You may want to discuss this with your academic/major advisor to explore alternative options or seek advice on finding a paid position for your experiential learning.  

<details>

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. ### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

In the context of Art & Media Studies major, a capstone is an individual project that demonstrates the principal learning outcomes and competencies of the curriculum. It could take the form of a thesis, an art work, or a film. The process of making a capstone typically involves the following steps:

1. Consult with your prospective advisor(s) early in your junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed project.
2. Begin the project, which may include initial stages of production (subject to your advisors’ approval).
3. Engage in active participation in the advising processes throughout the project.
4. Prepare an end-of-term submission at the end of Capstone I, which demonstrates successful progress towards the final Capstone submission. This submission may include a literature review or annotated bibliography of at least five pages, an introduction, and other materials/documents to be decided on in consultation with your advisors.
5. In Capstone II, focus more on production, whether it be writing your thesis or realizing a creative work or film.
6. Complete and submit the final Capstone project by the end of your senior year. The project should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking, and primary research, but should not require extensive fieldwork.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Art & Media Studies Capstone Handbook _v3_210125.pdf, Page: 6]
1. General Information: A culmination to the student’s curriculum, the capstone is an individual project that demonstrates the principal learning outcomes and competencies of that curriculum in a meaningful and coherent way. The capstone may also draw from relevant extra-curricular activities and practical experience to support the research and realization of the project. The capstone should evidence competency in a primary disciplinary specialization (optionally supported by secondary and tertiary disciplinary areas). In the Art & Media Studies major, the capstone could take the form of a thesis, an art work, or a film. For other kinds of projects, please consult with your prospective advisor(s) early in your junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed project. Remember, the capstone should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking, and we encourage primary research. However, it should not require extensive fieldwork. ### Question 72: What are the grades required to get a distinctive graduation?  
### Answer: 

To get a Pass With Honors, a student needs to score between 4.5 and 5.0 in the Total Average Score (weighted average of section scores). To get a Pass Without Honors, a student needs to score between 3.0 and 4.4. If a student scores 2.9 and below, they will not pass.

### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with Honor or have a high GPA, you need to maintain a 3.5 GPA throughout your academic career, especially during your senior year if you are applying for the capstone in Computer Science. You should also aim to earn good grades in your core courses and those that count towards your major/minor. If you receive a grade below 'C-' in a core course, you will be required to repeat it. Additionally, you should avoid receiving 'F', 'D+', 'D', 'W', or 'NP' grades as these will affect your GPA calculation. If you are unable to complete a course due to exceptional circumstances, you may be awarded a temporary 'I' grade, but you must complete the remaining course work within the agreed-upon timeframe to avoid receiving an 'F' grade. It is also important to note that the major faculty will assess capstone applicants based on their eligibility criteria and the quality of their proposal.  

<details>

### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 2 courses, 4 credits each, on a Pass/No Pass basis in one academic year. This is assuming that you are taking a 16-week term. The conditions apply that once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back. Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting to the P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis by completing a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form and submitting it to the Registrar’s Office before 4:00 PM on Friday Week 4 of the term (16-week term). ### Question 75: How many types of absences are there?  
### Answer: 

There are at least 8 types of absences mentioned in the context. These include general absences, military leave, excused absence due to university-sponsored events, emergency absences, personal leave, medical leave, administrative leave of absence, and absences due to other reasons not specified. However, it's possible that there are more types of absences not mentioned in the provided context.

### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence: Personal Leave, Medical Leave, and Administrative Leave of Absence. To have one, a student needs to consult with their Academic Advisor to plan for their learning path, complete and submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form, and provide supporting documents before the last day of class. The effective date of the Leave of Absence will be from the date of request submission if it’s approved.

Fulbright permits students in Good Academic Standing to apply for a leave of absence for one to two terms. Normally, a student is not permitted to remain on campus during a period of absence from their studies. Students may return earlier to Fulbright by notifying the Registrar’s Office at least eight (08) weeks in advance of the returning term. Students who return and resume their studies at Fulbright are expected to complete their program without further interruption. ### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic dishonesty, also known as Academic Integrity, is outlined in the Code of Academic Integrity. Violations of this policy, including the use of generative AI, are subject to the regulations described in this code. The policy is reviewed annually and any substantive changes are reviewed by the Dean’s Office and submitted to the Provost for approval. The approved policy is published and available in the One Stop portal.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

At the university, students are required to repeat core courses if they receive an F grade or if a course counted towards their major/minor receives a grade below 'C-'. Students may also repeat a course if they have received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or 'NP' for the course or have withdrawn and received a 'W' grade. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after receiving a grade higher than a 'D+' following consultation with their academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar's Office. If a student chooses to repeat a course, the higher grade will be used in the GPA calculation, while the lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP" and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. If a student wishes to dispute a final grade, they should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved, the student may file an appeal with the Registrar's Office within five business days from the date the final grade is posted. The appeal process involves an investigation by the Dean’s Office, and if necessary, a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>

Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. ### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university accommodates students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance by recognizing exceptional medical circumstances, close bereavement, victim of a serious crime, disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties, legal proceedings, and emergencies as exceptional circumstances. Students are responsible for submitting appropriate documentation and contacting their instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. Instructors are expected to allow the student to make up any missed assignments if the absence is reasonable and inform the student if they are in danger of failing the course because of class absence or missed assignments. Students are encouraged to discuss any unplanned absence or any known conflict with the course instructor(s) as soon as possible.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 17]
EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. This does not include everyday issues, e.g., traffic congestion, missed buses or trains. • Legal proceedings requiring

### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Yes, students can use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments, but they must follow the regulations described in Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity. Creative projects that incorporate generative AI must include comprehensive documentation covering every aspect of AI usage. This documentation should include the objective and scope, tools and platforms, process and methodology, and ethical and copyright issues associated with using generative AI. Students must also obtain Institutional Review Board (IRB) approval before the period of their Fulbright-affiliated research. Failure to do so may result in delays to the project and/or its suspension. It is recommended that students begin their IRB application as soon as their Capstone application is accepted, or during Capstone I at the latest. More information on the IRB approval process can be found at https://fulbright.edu.vn/irb/.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: VIETNAM STUDIES CAPSTONE GUIDELINES.pdf, Page: 6]
Clearly deﬁne the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the speciﬁc elements of the project it contributes to. • Tools and Platforms: Specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed. • Process and Methodology: Outline how AI will be incorporated, detailing which aspects of the project will be generated, improved, or altered with the use of AI. • Ethical and Copyright Issues: Address the ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI and how these will be addressed throughout the project. This comprehensive documentation promotes transparency, oﬀers insight into AI's role in the creative process, and highlights the originality and human contributions to the project. 1.8. Grading process All Capstones are graded by the primary and secondary advisor, using what is known as a double-marking process. 1.9. Group projects Group project proposals will be considered on a case-by-case basis. If the group project application is accepted, the primary and secondary advisors will decide on the

[Source: VIETNAM STUDIES CAPSTONE GUIDELINES.pdf, Page: 6]
approval process can be found at https://fulbright.edu.vn/irb/ 1.7. Academic Integrity The Capstone is subject to the regulations described in Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity, including updates on usage of generative AI. Creative projects involving generative AI will require full documentation of its usage. Creative projects that incorporate generative AI must include comprehensive documentation covering every aspect of AI usage. This documentation should include: • Objective and Scope: Clearly deﬁne the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the speciﬁc elements of the project it contributes to. • Tools and Platforms: Specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed. • Process and Methodology: Outline how AI will be incorporated, detailing which aspects of the project will be generated, improved, or altered with the use of AI. • Ethical and Copyright Issues: Address the ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI and how these will be addressed throughout

design and plan for data protection. Students must obtain IRB approval before the period of their Fulbright-aﬀiliated research. Failure to do so would result in delays to the project and/or its suspension. For this research,  students are advised to begin their IRB application as soon as their Capstone application is accepted, or during Capstone I (preferably week 7) at the latest. In any case, students should have their questionnaire ready and approved at the end of Capstone I. More information on the IRB approval process can be found at https://fulbright.edu.vn/irb/ 1.7. Academic Integrity The Capstone is subject to the regulations described in Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity, including updates on usage of generative AI. Creative projects involving generative AI will require full documentation of its usage. Creative projects that incorporate generative AI must include comprehensive documentation covering every aspect of AI usage. This documentation should include: • Objective and

[Source: Literature Capstone Handbook.pdf, Page: 8]
approval from Fulbright University Vietnam’s Institutional Review Board (IRB). The IRB approval process involves taking an online module to learn about IRB procedures, as well as submitting an application detailing your research design and plan for data protection. Students must obtain IRB approval before the period of their Fulbright-affiliated research. Failure to do so would result in delays to the project and/or its suspension. For this research,  students are advised to begin their IRB application as soon as their Capstone application is accepted, or during Capstone I at the latest. More information on the IRB approval process can be found at https://fulbright.edu.vn/irb/ 6 | P a g e 1.7. ### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer: 

You can find support for mental health treatment through various resources and projects. These include the Mental Health First Aid Training Program, Community Survey on Mental Health Needs, Public Art Project on Mental Health Themes, Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services, and Therapeutic Gardening or Nature Program. Additionally, you can develop your own project, such as a Peer Counseling Program or a Mental Health Workshop Series, in consultation with your academic advisors. Each project must include extensive documentation of the process through which the original work was developed and a final Evaluation Report that demonstrates the project’s relevance to psychological principles, its potential or observed impact, evidence of rigorous evaluation, and documentation of the student’s involvement and implementation of the program. The report should also provide insights or recommendations for future application or research.

### Question 85: Where can I find resources to facilitate my graduate program after Fulbright undergraduate?  
### Answer: 

Resources to facilitate your graduate program after Fulbright undergraduate can be found in several ways. First, Fulbright Vietnam Studies graduates will be prepared for graduate programs with a specific focus on Vietnam and related fields in universities around the world. Second, Fulbright has a student research fund which supports student’s research projects, including capstone. This fund can be applied for to fund the purchases of necessary resources for your graduate program. Third, if the necessary resources are not available at Fulbright, students and faculty can work together to find other institutions where FUV students could access the equipment. Lastly, if there is no viable way to get access to the equipment, changes to the experimental design might be necessary. Students should discuss with their advisors in such cases.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>

other universities. In earning a Fulbright bachelor’s degree in Vietnam Studies, strengthened by a specific disciplinary focus, plus language and interpersonal skills, students can confidently pursue a wide variety of careers where Vietnam stands at the center of an international network. For instance, they can work in the arts (including performance art and cinema), journalism, cultural and educational organizations, or research institutes.  They can also work for economic, diplomatic, or international institutions; tourism and commercial companies; and/or (non-)governmental organizations in Vietnam or overseas that require both broad and deep knowledge of the country. Vietnam Studies graduates will also be prepared for graduate programs with a specific focus on Vietnam and related fields in universities around the world. ### Question 87: Where can I get the assist for internship?  
### Answer: 

Assistance for internships can be obtained from the university's career services or placement office. They can help you find opportunities, prepare your application, and sometimes even connect you with potential employers. Additionally, industry mentors, who may be available for project guidance, could potentially provide information about internship opportunities in their respective industries. However, it's important to note that industry mentors are not primary advisors or independent reviewers for the capstone project.

### Question 88: How can I get the information of campus usage for events so that I can have proper place to study without getting interrupted?  
### Answer: 

To get information about campus usage for events and find a suitable place to study without interruptions, you should contact the relevant office or department that manages event scheduling at your university. This could be the Office of Student Activities, Event Management, or a similar department. They should be able to provide you with a schedule of upcoming events and help you find a quiet study space that is not being used for events during the times you need to study. Additionally, you can also check the university's online calendar for event listings and plan your study schedule accordingly.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

To transfer credit of studied courses at another university to your Fulbright undergraduate degree, you should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The required information may include course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit is justified. For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.

### Question 90: What are the policies of CWP?  
### Answer: 

The policies of CWP, as mentioned in the context, are not explicitly stated. However, it is known that the university-wide policy for passing a course is between 70-72.9% (1.7) and 73-76.9% (C). For additional requirements and exceptions, these should be made clear in the major's description and flowchart or handbook. Any exception to this policy must be approved by the major coordinator and the Dean’s Office.

### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you may be able to bypass some of the physical education courses required for graduation, depending on the specific rules of your athletic program and the university. However, it's important to note that physical education courses are typically not optional for most students, and you should consult with your academic advisor to understand the specific requirements for your program. Additionally, if you are an international student whose first language is not English, you will still be required to take an English Assessment Test as per NECHE Accreditation.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
• Physical Education • Political courses These courses do not count toward the 128-credit requirement. All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis by completing a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form and submitting it to the Registrar’s Office before 4:00 PM on Friday Week 4 of the term (16-week term).  The following conditions apply: o Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back. o Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses. They cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. o The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting to the P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. o A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. o Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to

### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

To register for a dormitory again, you would need to be reinstated as an "Active" status, which requires clearing any outstanding balance. If you anticipate being unable to clear the account on time, you should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. However, if you are on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) due to not registering in the returning term, you will need to confirm your plan to return by registering for course(s) or have been granted a leave extension, a maximum of another term. The extension must be endorsed by the Registrar's Office and approved by the Dean's Office. As for financial support, it's not explicitly mentioned in the context whether moving out of the dormitory affects financial aid eligibility. You should contact the Financial Aid Office for more information regarding your specific situation.

### Question 93: Can you give me the procedure to request for funds to support club activities?  
### Answer: 

To request funds for club activities, you would need to follow these steps:

1. Identify the specific funds required for your club activities.
2. Prepare a detailed budget outlining the expenses for the activities.
3. Write a proposal explaining the purpose of the activities, the benefits to the club and the university, and how the funds will be used.
4. Submit the proposal to the appropriate office at your university, such as the Student Activities Office or the Student Government Association.
5. Wait for a response. If approved, you will receive the funds and be required to provide receipts or other documentation to show how the funds were used.
6. If the funds are not sufficient, you may need to revise your budget or proposal, or explore other funding sources.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

The university provides support in several ways. Firstly, students have access to labs, tools, and software relevant to their project work. Support will be provided for learning new software or techniques where necessary. Secondly, mentorship may be available from industry mentors for project guidance, helping bridge academic learning and industry practice. They could be secondary advisors for Capstone projects, but not primary advisors or independent reviewers. They could also be invited to join the capstone panel. As either a secondary advisor or a member of the capstone panel, industry mentors could participate in grading. Lastly, there is limited funding available for materials and resources, and policies on budgeting and purchasing will be provided.

### Question 95: Can you give me the information about student fees and charges policy?  
### Answer: 

The fees and charges policy for undergraduate students at Fulbright University Vietnam can be found in the "Fees & Charges Guide" for undergraduate students. However, if a student experiences exceptional circumstances that impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, such as medical emergencies, close bereavement, or legal proceedings, tuition credit may be considered. No reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits. Students should be aware that course withdrawals may affect their financial aid eligibility if resulting in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment.

EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. ### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

If you believe that the professor's teaching methods do not meet academic standards, you should first discuss your concerns with the professor. If the issue remains unresolved, you may file an appeal with the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. The Registrar's Office will inform the Dean’s Office of the case, and if the Deans can mediate, no further action may be required. Otherwise, a panel review with the Dean’s Office will be organized for an independent evaluation of the situation. However, it's important to note that this process is primarily intended for disputes over final grades, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, not teaching methods. If you wish to provide feedback on the professor's teaching methods, you may consider using the university's feedback system, if available, or speaking with the department chair or academic advisor.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter.

### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

As a third year student, you should consult with your prospective advisor(s) early in your junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed capstone project. It's important to discuss your project idea with them to ensure it aligns with the capstone's purpose and your academic interests. You can find more information about the capstone project in section 1.3 of the Capstone project guidelines.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
The Capstone project is a year-long undertaking with less structure than a traditional course. It is certainly not the easiest way to complete your degree, and it may not be the most logical option for you, depending on your interests and your post-graduation plans. You should not consider it to be the default pathway to finishing your degree. One of the best reasons to undertake a Capstone project is if you enjoy doing historical research (which you will have sampled in Hands-On History and the research seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
projects Group project proposals will not be considered. The Capstone is intended as an individual undertaking and will be evaluated as such. There are other opportunities for group research. 1.8. Capstone I In Capstone I, you will actively conduct research and refine your project proposal and plan. You will focus on gathering and organizing your information or other materials needed to realize your project. In some cases, students may begin the very initial stages of production (subject to your advisors’ approval). Capstone I will be assessed by a combination of your active participation in the advising processes and end-of-term submission. The end-of-term submission will demonstrate successful progress towards the final Capstone submission, and satisfactory completion. Capstone I expectations: At the beginning of the semester, you should: • Meet with your advisor as early as possible. • Set a regular meeting schedule with your advisor. • Consult your advisor on the specific deliverables they expect to

[Source: Integrated Sciences_Capstone Handbook_14Jan2025.pdf, Page: 12]
purpose of the capstone. Students cannot re- use projects they did in previous years in place of the capstone. • Proposal for which there is no available facilities might be turned down. • Proposals for which there are no faculty with suitable expertise might be turned down. Students could find a secondary advisor at other institutions, more on this in section 1.3. At the undergraduate level, we are not expecting ground breaking work from students but the projects must be original and cannot be an exact repeat of previous works either from the student or from publised literature. This originality might take different forms such as different research subjects, different methodolgy or scopes…Students are strongly encouraged to discuss with IS faculty prior to submitting the capstone proposal. 1.3. Allocation of advisor process As part of the application process, applicants will provide a first choice of primary and secondary advisor. It is not mandatory to have a secondary advisor. After the applications are

[Source: Art & Media Studies Capstone Handbook _v3_210125.pdf, Page: 6]
1. General Information: A culmination to the student’s curriculum, the capstone is an individual project that demonstrates the principal learning outcomes and competencies of that curriculum in a meaningful and coherent way. The capstone may also draw from relevant extra-curricular activities and practical experience to support the research and realization of the project. The capstone should evidence competency in a primary disciplinary specialization (optionally supported by secondary and tertiary disciplinary areas). In the Art & Media Studies major, the capstone could take the form of a thesis, an art work, or a film. For other kinds of projects, please consult with your prospective advisor(s) early in your junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of your proposed project. Remember, the capstone should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking, and we encourage primary research. However, it should not require extensive fieldwork. You should think very carefully about an

do the work, and the sooner you are aware of them the better. The primary advisor would assess the deliverables from Capstone I and decide if the student passes. Only when a grade of “pass” is submitted by the primary advisor can the student be registered for Capstone II. If the students do not pass Capstone I, they should promptly plan their IS courses to fulfill the major requirements. 1.6. Capstone II In Capstone II you will focus mostly on conducting experiments, collecting data, doing analysis, and intepreting results. After getting results from each experiment, you should interpret how the results contribute to testing the hypotheses and answering the reseach question. Often the results of experiments would lead to futher testing, you should formulate your steps accordingly in consultation with your advisors. ### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

To attend the tournament, you should first submit a University Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form to the Dean’s Office. This form should be completed by your supervising staff (in this case, the coach of the basketball club). Keep Academic Affairs and Registrar’s Office in cc for the record. You will need to provide proof of your attendance at the tournament, such as an acceptance email or invitation letter, and proof of your travel, like flight and accommodation information/itinerary. After the tournament, you should write a reflection paper about your experience and submit it to ug.academic.affairs@fulbright.edu.vn within 7 days of your return.

Regarding the official transcript, you should contact the Registrar’s Office for assistance. They will guide you through the process of obtaining your transcript.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 13]
organizations (including but not limited to student athletes, student council presidents, student club members representing university, etc.). Only faculty or supervising staff can request the Excused Absence for students. The student is responsible for submitting appropriate documentation and contacting their instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. ### Question 101: How can I borrow books from the library?  
### Answer: 

The context does not provide information on how to borrow books from the library. However, it is common practice to visit the library, find the book you want, and check if it is available. If it is, you can usually borrow it by filling out a form and returning it within a specified time period. The specific procedures may vary depending on the library.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

To work with the major report in the context provided, you should follow these steps:

1. For Capstone by Applied and Creative Project, you need to submit an individual report on Canvas at least 7 days before the last day of the semester. The report should include a detailed description of the system or product, explanation of the setup and functionality, data and analysis of the outcomes, a summary of what has been achieved and the impact of your work, recommendations for further development or research, and documentation of the process.

2. For Capstone by Film or Media Production, the report should be a production book with writing about what students have researched, observed, experienced, solved, and lessons learned. The report should include all of the pre-production deliverables plus production documents, and the word count should be under 5000 words. The format can follow the thesis style guidelines.

3. For both Capstones, it is important to structure the Executive Summary in a specific way, as mentioned in the context.

4. For both Capstones, you should also check the formatting and referencing of your report, make sure each chapter starts on a new page, that your chapter numbering and Table of Contents are correct, that your Reference List and in-text citations are aligned, and that you have included the required Appendices (especially the documentation) as per the marking rubric.

5. Finally, once all necessary revisions have been made, the report should be converted into a single PDF document that is ready for submission.

Evaluation Reports The primary written deliverable for the Capstone by Applied and Creative Project is the Evaluation Report. The Evaluation Report includes • (1) the intellectual rationale of the project and its expected contributions to a given academic field within social studies, • * (2) the goals of the project, • (3) the evaluation questions regarding the degree to which the project met its goals, and • (4) a critical evaluation that answers the evaluation questions based on the documentation of the process (see below) and any data collected. Scoring of the evaluation report is based on the completeness, critical depth, intellectual rigor, and effective use of evidence and theory, not on whether the project appears to have met its goals. The appendix of the Evaluation Report includes documentation of the process, consisting of relevant research, material experimentation, timelines, documentary photographs of the

### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

You can fulfill the Experiential Learning (EL) requirements in two ways:

1. By completing at least 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits from the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) as a graduation requirement. The ELP is housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI).

2. If your advisor approves, Experiential Learning can also count toward your elective courses or major requirements. However, it's important to note that certain courses may not count toward the 8-credit limit if they are not cross-listed between your major and the source major, or if they are not 'tagged' in interdisciplinary minors. For more details, please refer to the link provided.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: CS_Capstone_Guideline_v2_Dec_20_2024.pdf, Page: 2]
2. Eligibility criteria ..................................................................................................................... 1:

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
count toward elective or major requirements (upon advisor approval). Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. For more details, please refer here https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/s/article/Experiential-Learning- Program 13.5  Electives To complete the degree, students are free to take elective courses from the Course Catalogue.
